                  <form>       
                     <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حرّمهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حرم</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حرمه</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حرمة</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَحْرِيمٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) said of God, (K,) and of a man, (S, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He forbade it, prohibited it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made it unlawful,</hi> (S, Msb, K, *) <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">to him;</hi> (S;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n7754-1" target="احرمهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, * Msb, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">إِحْرَامٌ</foreign>. (S.) The saying <foreign lang="ar">اَللّٰهُ أَكْبَرُ</foreign> at the commencement of prayer is termed <foreign lang="ar">تَكْبِيرَةُ التَّحْرِيمِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تكبيرة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of prohibition</hi>], because it prohibits the person praying from saying and doing anything extraneous to prayer: and it is also termed   
      <foreign lang="ar">تكبيرةُ <ref cref="n7754-2" target="الإِحْرَامِ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تكبيرة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">of entering upon a state of prohibition</hi> by prayer. (TA.) It is said in a trad., of Ibn- 'Abbás, <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا حَرَّمَ الرَّجُلُ ٱمْرَأَتَهُ فَهِىَ يَمِينٌ يُكَفِّرُهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">When the man declares his wife to be forbidden to him, it is an oath, which he must expiate</hi>]: for the <foreign lang="ar">تَحْرِيم</foreign> of a wife and of a female slave may be without the intention of divorce. (TA.)
